  <a href="/user/show/8084339-alana" class="left imgcol" title="Alana"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1394312036p2/8084339.jpg" alt="Alana" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1357021333?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 19, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8084339-alana" class="user" title="Alana">Alana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/176000.The_Cider_House_Rules" title="Paperback 9780345417947" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8084339-alana?shelf=books-to-film" class="actionLinkLite">books-to-film</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8084339-alana?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8084339-alana?shelf=political" class="actionLinkLite">political</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8084339-alana?shelf=boxall-s-1001-books" class="actionLinkLite">boxall-s-1001-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8084339-alana?shelf=christian-reading" class="actionLinkLite">christian-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1357021333">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5098576735022090781">This is one I had to sit and mull over for a while after I finished it. This book is so full of thought-provoking situations and circumstances that it's hard to sum it all down to a little book review. On the surface, it seems that it's merely a book about abortion, and why it should or shouldn't be legal. But that would be doing a great disservice to the book. It is about family, and what a family is truly made of. Does blood make one family, or is it something deeper than that? It's love betwe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5098576735022090781">This is one I had to sit and mull over for a while after I finished it. This book is so full of thought-provoking situations and circumstances that it's hard to sum it all down to a little book review. On the surface, it seems that it's merely a book about abortion, and why it should or shouldn't be legal. But that would be doing a great disservice to the book. It is about family, and what a family is truly made of. Does blood make one family, or is it something deeper than that? It's love between those that don't know how to express it well. It's courage to do something that you believe is right, even when society disagrees. It's courage to NOT do what you believe is NOT right, even when it goes against the grain of those who love you most and (think they) know you best. It's the consequences of action and inaction, both the long and short term. <br /><br />I would give this book five stars, except for a key point in the end, when a character goes against his own beliefs to do something believed to be for the greater good. To me, it cannot be for the greater good to do something that you believe in your soul to not be right. Contradicting your own self cannot be the starting point for a better society.<br /><br />Other than that, the questions raised and ideas provoked in this story make it one well worth reading. <br />4.5/5</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5098576735022090781">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_30384259">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30384259" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/637062-jacob" class="left imgcol" title="Jacob"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1291085023p2/637062.jpg" alt="Jacob" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/30384259?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/637062-jacob" class="user" title="Jacob">Jacob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/23249714-the-cider-house-rules" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/637062-jacob?shelf=fiction-and-literature" class="actionLinkLite">fiction-and-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/637062-jacob?shelf=i-own" class="actionLinkLite">i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/637062-jacob?shelf=2007-2009" class="actionLinkLite">2007-2009</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/637062-jacob?shelf=irving-james-melville" class="actionLinkLite">irving-james-melville</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer30384259">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16835070120599185209">November 2009<br /><blockquote>What is hardest to accept about the passage of time is that the people who once mattered the most to us are wrapped up in parentheses.<br />(<u>The Cider House Rules</u>, p. 429)</blockquote><br /><br />In 19__, when abortion was still illegal (when women who did not want their babies were criminals; when pregnancy was a sentence <em>and</em> a fine), there were still ways to avoid the accident of birth: there were medicines and various chemicals to gamble with, or else there were grim back-room doctors, butchers, and other shad</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16835070120599185209">November 2009<br /><blockquote>What is hardest to accept about the passage of time is that the people who once mattered the most to us are wrapped up in parentheses.<br />(<u>The Cider House Rules</u>, p. 429)</blockquote><br /><br />In 19__, when abortion was still illegal (when women who did not want their babies were criminals; when pregnancy was a sentence <em>and</em> a fine), there were still ways to avoid the accident of birth: there were medicines and various chemicals to gamble with, or else there were grim back-room doctors, butchers, and other shady figures with even shadier credentials. From them, the price for an abortion was often your dignity, your freedom, or even (and all-too-occasionally) your life. <br /><br />Or you could have made the pilgrimage to the orphanage at St. Cloud’s, to see Dr. Larch--who would give you an abortion (or deliver an orphan) free of charge; the only cost was the knowing glare of the stationmaster when you stepped off the train, and the long pre-dawn walk up the hill to the hospital. If you had looked up during your walk (and you wouldn’t have looked up), you may have seen an insomniac orphan or two watching from the windows--but the price of <em>that</em> would be too great.<br /><br />And if you went to St. Cloud’s for an abortion (or an orphan) in the years leading up to the War--the second one--then you may have met Homer Wells, the orphan no one could keep, the one who always came back to St. Cloud’s, the one who would eventually become “of use” to Dr. Larch. Perhaps Homer helped you: perhaps Homer delivered your orphan (he would not have performed an abortion). You may have wondered what would become of him, after you were long gone from St. Cloud’s (and if you did not get pregnant again). Was he just an assistant? Was he another doctor--was he Dr. Larch’s successor to the orphanage?<br /><br />Of course, you may not have met Homer at all when you were there: he was only “of use” for a short time. He was just an orphan before that (and you would try not to notice the orphans), and later--shortly before, during, and long after the War--he was not there at all. Unless you caught the nurses in idle gossip (or if Dr. Larch had mentioned him--and he wouldn’t), you would never have heard about him. But if you did, if you overheard how much Homer Wells was missed by the orphanage, and how much Dr. Larch loved him, you may have wondered what became of this orphan who was too old to be adopted. Where was he? What had happened to him? Perhaps he <em>had</em> been adopted--at last. Perhaps Homer Wells had found a family.<br /><br />...<br /><br />Too much punctuation?<br /><br />Yeah, too much punctuation.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16835070120599185209">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_37273193">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37273193" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1697661-sarah" class="left imgcol" title="Sarah"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Sarah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/37273193?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 03, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1697661-sarah" class="user" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/4687.The_Cider_House_Rules" title="Hardcover 9780786226740" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer37273193">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18089034204304445609">Over all a pretty crappy book. There were some good points. There were some very powerful and strong characters, and then some really flat see-through personalities. Ultimately the book had a very good point. Everyone makes rules, and as people we have to pick which ones we follow and which ones we don't. Should we follow rules? Should we make our own rules? How relevant and practical are actual rules in the real world? More specifically, how relevant are ant-abortion laws? As the readers we tak</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18089034204304445609">Over all a pretty crappy book. There were some good points. There were some very powerful and strong characters, and then some really flat see-through personalities. Ultimately the book had a very good point. Everyone makes rules, and as people we have to pick which ones we follow and which ones we don't. Should we follow rules? Should we make our own rules? How relevant and practical are actual rules in the real world? More specifically, how relevant are ant-abortion laws? As the readers we take two journey's, one as the doctor, who learns when to bend the rules for ethical reasons. We also watch young Homer as he learns about the purpose of rules. Ultimately though, it is the character of Melanie, who I feel is the hero of the story. Melanie, despite appearing to be mildly sociopathic, seems to be the only one holding any integrity and morals. In the end she gives Homer a good kick in the ass as she sees he has essentially disowned his own son. It saddens me her character was completely taken out of the movie. The character I hated the most was Candy. Candy is a character clearly invented by a man, for men. She seems to have no other emotions but being helplessly attracted to men. She never objects to any thing anyone does, her emotions are never considered, except that she desires men, and can’t chose between them. When Homer takes a pregnant Candy away from her family to endure pregnancy and birth with a bunch of strangers, Candy never seems to mind. Not even during Christmas does she mind being held in hiding from her father whom she is very close too, and her friends and close family. She is just simply there pleasantly happy. <br />The book is badly written. There is often foreshadowing for something that never happens, as if author took out large chunks of plot, but forgot to go back and edit it. Candy isn't the only flat character, and there's a lot of useless information about things that don't really add to the plot, or have to do with anything. Often there are scenes, words that are extremely disturbing. This would be fine if these awful scenes contributed to story, or plot, or were interesting, or placed in strategic places. Instead they are there merely to make the reader uncomfortable. For example, the whole pornographic picture with the woman and the horse, is that really necessary to explain about Homer's sexual development and Melanie’s violence? Or must we really hear the details about Candy getting shaved before her abortion, and how Homer saved her hair? These scenes distract from the plot, leave a bad taste, ultimately painting the world as a crude, awkward, unnatural place. Perhaps that is how Irving sees the world, and this book is his betrayal. That's interesting.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18089034204304445609">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_182864996">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182864996" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/285565-rebecca" class="left imgcol" title="Rebecca"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1315260462p2/285565.jpg" alt="Rebecca" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/182864996?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 14, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/285565-rebecca" class="user" title="Rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer182864996">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16305593434211901984">This is the third of Irving's novels I've read (the other two being <em>The World According to Garp</em> and <em>A Widow for One Year</em>), and I think I'm about done with Irving now. None of those three books were outright bad, but each one started with such promise and ultimately ended up disappointing me.<br /><br />Irving is really skilled at writing about tragedy, awkwardness, sexual entanglements, and grief, in particular. He has a gift for describing emotions, dialogue, and social interaction extremely realistically.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16305593434211901984">This is the third of Irving's novels I've read (the other two being <em>The World According to Garp</em> and <em>A Widow for One Year</em>), and I think I'm about done with Irving now. None of those three books were outright bad, but each one started with such promise and ultimately ended up disappointing me.<br /><br />Irving is really skilled at writing about tragedy, awkwardness, sexual entanglements, and grief, in particular. He has a gift for describing emotions, dialogue, and social interaction extremely realistically. There were several moments in <em>Cider House Rules</em> that he handled perfectly. <br /><br />However, my own personal opinion is that Irving lets his stories get too big and they end up losing focus and not "saying" very much to the reader. Without spoiling anything about this book, I'll just say that some of the subplots in the story were purely decorative, some of story developments didn't seem important enough to be in the narrative, and one of the biggest revelations in the story was handled pretty anticlimactically. <br /><br />Also -- and this is a much smaller complaint, but I feel like I should mention it because it really did reduce the amount of pleasure I got out of the book -- certain aspects of Irving's writing REALLY get on my nerves. The nearly constant use of dashes and semicolons broke up the text too much, the repeated use of characters' first and last names several times on the same page was clunky and monotonous, and the main character's not-so-endearing verbal tic was extremely aggravating (so aggravating, in fact, that even several other characters within the novel remarked on how annoying it was). Novels (especially long ones) are like roommates: they might be wonderful, but sometimes the littlest quirks and habits can drive you up the wall if you spend a long enough time with them.<br /><br />I haven't seen the movie adaptation of this book yet, but I cannot for the life of me imagine Michael Caine playing the role of Dr. Larch. Maybe that's because I can only picture him as Alfred from the <em>Batman</em> movies.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16305593434211901984">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1298579689">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1298579689" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6326169-negin" class="left imgcol" title="Negin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450512230p2/6326169.jpg" alt="Negin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1298579689?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6326169-negin" class="user" title="Negin">Negin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/4687.The_Cider_House_Rules" title="Hardcover 9780786226740" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1298579689">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9237794775769910056">I really, really wanted to like this book, and I thought it was very good initially, but the more I read, the less I liked it. Unlike many others, the subject matter (abortion) didn’t bother me at all. What bothered me was an overall lack of connection with the characters and the fact that I honestly felt that this more than 600 page book was never going to end! I think that he could have written this in 300 pages or less. I found myself frequently checking to see how much there was left to read</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9237794775769910056">I really, really wanted to like this book, and I thought it was very good initially, but the more I read, the less I liked it. Unlike many others, the subject matter (abortion) didn’t bother me at all. What bothered me was an overall lack of connection with the characters and the fact that I honestly felt that this more than 600 page book was never going to end! I think that he could have written this in 300 pages or less. I found myself frequently checking to see how much there was left to read. <br />One thing that annoys me quite a bit with Irving is his obsession with weight, specifically, with regards to women and weight. It seems to be a major issue with him. I don’t like that sort of crap at all. Many years ago, I read a terrible book by him, “The 158-Pound Marriage”, named after one of the characters who weighed the “dreaded” 158-pounds. How could she?! Quelle horreur! To be that obese! The story line for that one was the absolute worst – about two couples who swapped partners, swingers basically. <br />I’m giving it two stars, because I feel a wee bit generous and because I have to be honest in that I liked it at first. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9237794775769910056">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <a href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska" class="user" title="Elizabeth (Alaska)">Elizabeth (Alaska)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16095003-the-cider-house-rules" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=1001-books" class="actionLinkLite">1001-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=new-england" class="actionLinkLite">new-england</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=late-20th-century" class="actionLinkLite">late-20th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer247393061">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3117454109702765244">Average rating on GR is above 4 stars, and many of my friends rated this one 5 stars. I was glad to finally get to it.<br /><br />I must have read a different book. I don't know what everyone sees in this. The prose, while not exactly boring, isn't very interesting either. Except for the medical terminology, the vocabulary is rather simple, and the sentence structure leaves much to be desired. I admit that I feel the same for much of contemporary fiction, so my reaction should not be laid completely at the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3117454109702765244">Average rating on GR is above 4 stars, and many of my friends rated this one 5 stars. I was glad to finally get to it.<br /><br />I must have read a different book. I don't know what everyone sees in this. The prose, while not exactly boring, isn't very interesting either. Except for the medical terminology, the vocabulary is rather simple, and the sentence structure leaves much to be desired. I admit that I feel the same for much of contemporary fiction, so my reaction should not be laid completely at the door of John Irving. I found the characterizations not especially good, although, to be fair, they are a bit more than flat or one-dimensional.<br /><br />My biggest problem is the subject matter. I agree with Irving on the subject of choice. Unfortunately, he chose to think that he had to hit people over the head on the subject. Since I already agreed with him, the club was unnecessary. It has been my experience that presenting an argument on a controversial subject in the manner of clubbing him will never sway opinion. The dissenters will just become more firmly entrenched, and those in agreement were, well, already in agreement.<br /><br />I reserve 1-star for books I couldn't finish or for those I truly hated - like Swift's Gulliver's Travels. This wasn't as bad as that, but pretty close.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3117454109702765244">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_863856187">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863856187" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2819998-scarlett-rains" class="left imgcol" title="Scarlett Rains"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1317235331p2/2819998.jpg" alt="Scarlett Rains" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/863856187?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2819998-scarlett-rains" class="user" title="Scarlett Rains">Scarlett Rains</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/4687.The_Cider_House_Rules" title="Hardcover 9780786226740" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2819998-scarlett-rains?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2819998-scarlett-rains?shelf=scarlett-s-reviews" class="actionLinkLite">scarlett-s-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer863856187">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14306748507713258052">The Cider House Rules by John Irving provides insight into the painful, politically charged, topic of abortion. Homer, an abandoned orphan, is the champion of life and finds the idea of abortion repugnant. Wilbur, the surgeon Homer considers father and mentor, feels passionately that a woman must have the right to choose. Each man sways us. <br /><br />The emotional devastation wrought by the abandonment of unwanted children is sensitively told. We imagine the orphans waiting for adoptive parents, listening</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14306748507713258052">The Cider House Rules by John Irving provides insight into the painful, politically charged, topic of abortion. Homer, an abandoned orphan, is the champion of life and finds the idea of abortion repugnant. Wilbur, the surgeon Homer considers father and mentor, feels passionately that a woman must have the right to choose. Each man sways us. <br /><br />The emotional devastation wrought by the abandonment of unwanted children is sensitively told. We imagine the orphans waiting for adoptive parents, listening for the sound of cars in the lane…hoping, crying when other children are adopted. We feel Wilbur’s pain as he remembers patients dying in anguish from sepsis after tortuous attempted abortions from unskilled charlatans. <br /><br />Irving crafts a human story, beautifully told, of ordinary people confronted by difficult decisions. He presents the perspectives of women caught in situations beyond their control, making it difficult for the reader to remain neutral on the subject. We are drawn in, slipping on the razor’s edge of the moral question of abortion as Candy, Grace, Lorna and Rose Rose tell their tales. We consider our view on abortion as we examine their predicaments. Is abortion, regardless of any circumstance, murder? Is it cruel to create unwanted orphans that are likely to be neglected and abused rather than to abort a fetus? Should a woman have sovereignty over her body? Irving seems to be asking us to consider these questions, and more. <br /><br />When faced with unwanted pregnancy, a woman chooses her rules according to her moral or religious code. The reader may not condone abortion but, after reading this book, must acknowledge that the decision to abort is not always an act of irresponsibly selfish women choosing a frivolous method of birth control. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14306748507713258052">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sh8RWC/jSr9yVTv2QT/zdIrwa9VazzU620twMBl4JefXyy6L3TFeRf6NT00/XhXGwweozBMScpCxQnWi1e3Tog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FGuLytkISYo5FeHJAar3jjKVqMNOOsKvNWbKgeSAFKFxv7QZK9pdcLXNlXJ/yxE8e2Jr2gfnhQVfb88TKBXi5A==')})
  }

It is Zuckerman who stumbles upon Silk\'s secret and sets out to reconstruct the unknown biography of this eminent, upright man, esteemed as an educator for nearly all his life, and to understand how this ingeniously contrived life came unraveled.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3075.John_Irving">About John Irving</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3075.John_Irving"><img alt="3075" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1257375547p2/3075.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1857413394429166900">JOHN IRVING was born in Exeter, New Hampshire, in 1942. His first novel, Setting Free the Bears, was published in 1968, when he was twenty-six. He competed as a wrestler for twenty years, and coached wrestling until he was forty-seven.<br /> Mr. Irving has been nominated for a National Book Award three times—winning once, in 1980, for his novel The World According to Garp. He received an O. Henry Award</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1857413394429166900">JOHN IRVING was born in Exeter, New Hampshire, in 1942. His first novel, Setting Free the Bears, was published in 1968, when he was twenty-six. He competed as a wrestler for twenty years, and coached wrestling until he was forty-seven.<br />	Mr. Irving has been nominated for a National Book Award three times—winning once, in 1980, for his novel The World According to Garp. He received an O. Henry Award in 1981 for his short story “Interior Space.” In 2000, Mr. Irving won the Oscar for Best Adapted Screenplay for The Cider House Rules. In 2013, he won a Lambda Literary Award for his novel In One Person.<br />	An international writer—his novels have been translated into more than thirty-five languages—John Irving lives in Toronto. His all-time best-selling novel, in every language, is A Prayer for Owen Meany. <br />	Avenue of Mysteries is his fourteenth novel. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1857413394429166900">...more</a>

    </div>

    n = load.length,
    i = 0,
    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i &lt; n; i += 1) {
        script = d.createElement('SCRIPT');
        script.type = 'text/javascript';
        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
